<tr style="display:none">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>East Asia</b> is the eastern <a href="/wiki/Subregion" title="Subregion">subregion</a> of the Asian continent, which can be defined in either <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geographical</a><sup id="cite_ref-encarta-east-asia_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-east-asia-5">[3]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Cultural" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural">pan-ethno-cultural</a><sup id="cite_ref-easia-columbia_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-easia-columbia-6">[4]</a></sup> terms. Geographically and geopolitically, it includes China (including Hong Kong and Macau), Mongolia, North Korea, South Korea, Japan and Taiwan; it covers about 12,000,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,600,000&#160;sq&#160;mi), or about 28% of the Asian continent. GDP(PPP) of East Asia is 32.4 trillion while Nominal GDP is 19.1 trillion USD.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/East_Asian_people" title="East Asian people">East Asians</a> comprise around 1.6 billion people. About 38% of the population of Asia and 22%, or over one fifth, of world's population lives in East Asia. Although the coastal and riparian areas of the region form one of the world's most populated places, the population in <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_China" title="Western China">Western China</a>, both landlocked areas, is very sparsely distributed, with Mongolia having the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">lowest population density of a sovereign state</a>. The overall <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of the region is 133 inhabitants per square kilometre (340/sq&#160;mi), about three times the world average of 45/km<sup>2</sup> (120/sq&#160;mi).</p>
<p>Historically, societies in East Asia have been part of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cultural_sphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese cultural sphere">Chinese cultural sphere</a>, and East Asian vocabulary and scripts are often derived from <a href="/wiki/Classical_Chinese" title="Classical Chinese">Classical Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_character" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese character">Chinese script</a>. Major religions include <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana</a><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[5]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Neo-Confucianism" title="Neo-Confucianism">Neo-Confucianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">Chinese folk religion</a> in China and Taiwan, <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">Shinto</a> in Japan, <a href="/wiki/Korean_shamanism" title="Korean shamanism">Korean shamanism</a> in Korea. <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">Shamanism</a> is also prevalent among <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolians</a> and other indigenous populations of northern East Asia such as the Manchus and Ewenki.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> Islam is popular in <a href="/wiki/Northwest_China" title="Northwest China">Northwest China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Mongolia" title="Islam in Mongolia">Kazaks in Mongolia</a>.The <a href="/wiki/Chinese_calendar" title="Chinese calendar">Chinese calendar</a> is the root from which many other East Asian calendars are derived.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_East_Asia" title="History of East Asia">History of East Asia</a></div>
<p>The Chinese Dynasties dominated this region culturally and militarily for a lengthy period of time. Cultural and religious exchange between the Chinese and other regional East Asian Dynasties and Kingdoms occurred.</p>
<p>As connections with the Western world strengthened, China's power began to diminish. Around the same time, Japan solidified itself as a nation state. During World War II, Korea, Taiwan, much of eastern China, Hong Kong, and Vietnam all fell under Japanese control. Following Japan's defeat in the war, the Korean peninsula became independent but then it was divided into <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Korea" class="mw-redirect" title="Partition of Korea">two rival states</a>, while Taiwan became the main territory of de facto state <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Republic of China">Republic of China</a> after the latter lost mainland China to the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_Statistics_Division">United Nations Statistics Division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: United Nations Statistics Division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/250px-East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" width="250" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/375px-East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/500px-East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Asia_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
East Asia map of Köppen climate classification.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png/250px-Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png" width="250" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png/375px-Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png/500px-Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png 2x" data-file-width="527" data-file-height="412" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Location-Asia-UNsubregions.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/UNSD" class="mw-redirect" title="UNSD">UNSD</a> geoscheme for Asia based on statistic convenience rather than implying any assumption regarding political or other affiliation of countries or territories:<sup id="cite_ref-auto_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-10">[8]</a></sup>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000E0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E000E0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00E000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E00000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFFF20; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<b>East Asia</b></div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFC000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">UNSD</a> definition of East Asia is based on statistical convenience,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-10">[8]</a></sup> but also other common definitions of East Asia contain the entirety of <a href="/wiki/Greater_China" title="Greater China">China</a> (including Mainland China, Hong Kong, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>) Mongolia, North Korea, South Korea, Japan and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-encarta-east-asia_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-east-asia-5">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_regions_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_regions-11">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Culturally, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Japan" title="Culture of Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Korea" title="Culture of Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Taiwan" title="Culture of Taiwan">Taiwan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Vietnam" title="Culture of Vietnam">Vietnam</a> are commonly seen as being encompassed by <b>cultural East Asia</b> (<a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">East Asian cultural sphere</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-easia-columbia_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-easia-columbia-6">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_definitions">Alternative definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Alternative definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are mixed debates around the world whether these countries or regions should be considered in East Asia or not.</p>
<ul>
<li>Vietnam (officially part of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> geographically, although culturally it is a part of the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">East Asian cultural sphere</a>, politically, it is related to both <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> and East Asia)</li>
<li>Siberia in Russia (often described as <a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">North Asia</a> due to its location, although this part of Russia is often seen as more closely related to its East Asian neighbours)</li>
<li>Sovereignty issues exist over some <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea_Islands" title="South China Sea Islands">territories in the South China Sea</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>In business and economics, "East Asia" is sometimes used to refer to a wide geographical area covering ten <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> countries in <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" class="mw-redirect" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>, Taiwan, Japan and South Korea. However, in this context, the term "Far East" is often more appropriate which covers ASEAN countries and the countries in East Asia. However, being a Eurocentric term, <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a> describes the region's geographical position in relation to Europe rather than its location within Asia. Alternatively, the term "<a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia Pacific Region</a>" is often used in describing East Asia, Southeast Asia as well as <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.</p>
<p>Observers preferring a broader definition of "East Asia" often use the term <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Asia" title="Northeast Asia">Northeast Asia</a> to refer to the greater China area, Taiwan, the Korean Peninsula, and Japan, with <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> covering the ten <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" class="mw-redirect" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> countries. This usage, which is seen in economic and diplomatic discussions, is at odds with the historical meanings of both "East Asia" and "Northeast Asia".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Council_on_Foreign_Relations" title="Council on Foreign Relations">Council on Foreign Relations</a> defines Northeast Asia as Japan and Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-Northeast_Asia_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northeast_Asia-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_East_Asia" title="Economy of East Asia">Economy of East Asia</a></div>
<p>The economy of East Asia is one of the most developed and high-tech economies of the world, being home to some of the world's largest, most technologically advanced, productive and most prosperous economies such as the <a href="/wiki/Industrialized" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialized">industrialized</a> <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a> of South Korea, Taiwan, and Japan. Major positive factors have ranged from favorable political-legal environments for industry and commerce, through abundant natural resources of various kinds, to plentiful supplies of relatively low-cost, skilled and adaptable labor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In modern high-technology dependent societies, a high level of structural differentiation, functional specialization, and autonomy of the economic system from an efficient government is a major contributor to industrial-commercial growth and prosperity. Currently in East Asia, trading systems are relatively open; and zero or low duties on imports of consumer and capital goods etc. have considerably helped stimulate cost-efficiency and change. Free and flexible labor and other markets are other important factors making for high levels of business-economic performance. East Asian populations have demonstrated highly positive work ethics. There are relatively large and fast-growing markets for consumer goods and services of all kinds.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_cultural_sphere" title="East Asian cultural sphere">East Asian cultural sphere</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The culture of East Asia has largely been <a href="/wiki/Sinicization" title="Sinicization">influenced</a> by <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">China</a>, as it was the civilization that had the most dominant influence in the region throughout the ages.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> Evidence of this can be seen in the adoption of Confucian ethical philosophy, architectural style, diet, lexicon, Buddhism, political and legal systems, and historically a common <a href="/wiki/Written_Chinese" title="Written Chinese">writing system</a> reflected in the histories of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_writing_system" title="Japanese writing system">Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korean_writing_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean writing system">Korea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reischauer_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reischauer-46">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> The Imperial Chinese tributary system was the bedrock of network of trade and foreign relations between China and its East Asian tributaries, which helped to shape much of East Asian affairs during the ancient and medieval eras. Through the tributary system, the various dynasties of Imperial China facilitated frequent economic and cultural exchange that influenced the cultures of Japan and Korea and drew them into a <a href="/wiki/Sinocentrism" title="Sinocentrism">Chinese international order</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The Imperial Chinese tributary system shaped much of East Asia's foreign policy and trade for over 2000 years due to Imperial China's economic and cultural dominance over the region, and thus played a huge role in the history of East Asia in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> The relationship between China and it's cultural influence on East Asia has been compared to the historical influence of <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_civilization" class="mw-redirect" title="Greco-Roman civilization">Greco-Roman civilization</a> on Europe and the Western World.<sup id="cite_ref-Reischauer_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reischauer-46">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions">Religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaboration">Collaboration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Collaboration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Asian_Youth_Games">East Asian Youth Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: East Asian Youth Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Formerly the <a href="/wiki/East_Asian_Games" title="East Asian Games">East Asian Games</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> organised by the East Asian Games Association (EAGA) and held every four years since <a href="/wiki/2019_East_Asian_Youth_Games" title="2019 East Asian Youth Games">2019</a> among athletes from East Asian countries and territories of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Council_of_Asia" title="Olympic Council of Asia">Olympic Council of Asia</a> (OCA), as well as the Pacific island of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, which is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oceania_National_Olympic_Committees" title="Oceania National Olympic Committees">Oceania National Olympic Committees</a>.</p>
<p>The East Asian Games is 1 of 5 Regional Games of the OCA. The others are the East Asian Games, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_Games" title="Central Asian Games">Central Asian Games</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Games" title="South Asian Games">South Asian Games</a>, the<a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games" title="Southeast Asian Games">Southeast Asian Games</a> (SEA Games), and the <a href="/wiki/West_Asian_Games" title="West Asian Games">West Asian Games</a>. All nigh East Asian States/Territories join this Game.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup></p>

href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia"><img alt="Mongolia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Mongolia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mongolia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan"><img alt="Taiwan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Republic_of_China.svg.png" width="23" <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities_and_towns">Major cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Major cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cities_of_East_Asia" title="Cities of East Asia">Cities of East Asia</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 703px;_width: 703px;">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:50px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg/660px-Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg" width="660" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg/990px-Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg/1320px-Tokyo_at_night_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8492" data-file-height="1936" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> is the largest city in the world, both in <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of metropolitan areas by population">metropolitan population</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP#List_of_cities_in_the_world_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">economy</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:70px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg/660px-Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg" width="660" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg/990px-Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg/1320px-Seoul_360%C2%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="23886" data-file-height="3973" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a> is the capital of South Korea, one of the largest cities in the world and a leading global technology hub.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg/560px-Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg" width="560" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg/839px-Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Pyonyang_from_Yanggakdo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="403" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Pyongyang" title="Pyongyang">Pyongyang</a> is the capital of <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> (DPRK), and is a significant metropolis on the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg/331px-Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg" width="331" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg/497px-Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg/663px-Shanghaiviewpic4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> is the largest city in China (People's Republic of China) and one of the largest in the world, and is the leading business and financial centre of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Taipei-Night_view.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taipei-Night_view.jpg/330px-Taipei-Night_view.jpg" width="330" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taipei-Night_view.jpg/495px-Taipei-Night_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taipei-Night_view.jpg/660px-Taipei-Night_view.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="640" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a> is the <i>de facto</i> capital of Taiwan (formally known as the Republic of China), and is one of the world's leading technical centres in East Asia, and is the location of the <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg/625px-Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg" width="625" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg/938px-Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg/1250px-Hong_Kong_Night_Skyline2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4670" data-file-height="1644" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, enclosed by the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River Delta</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>, is one of the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">global financial centres</a> and is known as a cosmopolitan metropolis.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 695px">
<div style="width: 695px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 690px;">
<div style="margin:30px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg/660px-Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg" width="660" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg/990px-Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/Ulan_Bator_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="328" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" title="Ulaanbaatar">Ulaanbaatar</a> is the largest city in Mongolia with a population of 1 million as of 2008.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>

Pass of the ISS over Mongolia, looking out west towards the Pacific Ocean, China, and Japan. As the video progresses, you can see major cities along the coast and the Japanese islands on the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Sea" title="Philippine Sea">Philippine Sea</a>. The island of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> can be seen further down the pass into the Philippine Sea, and the pass ends just to the east of New Zealand. A lightning storm can be seen as light pulses near the end of the video.</div>
